## Error Analysis and Resolution

### Error 1: Inconsistent patch and patchField types for `bottom`

**Error Message:**
```
inconsistent patch and patchField types for 
    patch type symmetryPlane and patchField type zeroGradient
```

**Root Cause:**
The `bottom` boundary is defined as `symmetryPlane` type in `blockMeshDict`, but in the `0/T` file, the `bottom` boundary condition is set to `zeroGradient`. OpenFOAM requires that when a patch is declared as `symmetryPlane` type in the mesh, the corresponding boundary condition in all field files must also be `symmetryPlane`.

**Solution:**
In the `0/T` file, change the `bottom` boundary condition from `zeroGradient` to `symmetryPlane`:

```
bottom
{
    type            symmetryPlane;
}
```

This must be done consistently across **all** field files (`0/U`, `0/T`, `0/p`) to ensure compatibility with the `symmetryPlane` patch type defined in `blockMeshDict`.

### Error 2: Cannot find `setFieldsDict`

**Error Message:**
```
cannot find file "system/setFieldsDict"
```

**Root Cause:**
The `rhoCentralFoam` solver requires a `setFieldsDict` file in the `system/` directory to initialize the flow field. This file tells the solver how to set up initial and boundary conditions for the first time step.

**Solution:**
Create a `system/setFieldsDict` file. Based on the obliqueShock tutorial and the user's specifications, the file should define the initial conditions for `U`, `T`, and `p`. A minimal example would be:

```
FoamFile
{
    version     2.0;
    format      ascii;
    class       dictionary;
    location    "system";
    object      setFieldsDict;
}

backgroundField   uniform (2.9 0 0);

patches
{
    inlet
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform (2.9 0 0);
    }

    outlet
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform (2.9 0 0);
    }

    top
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform (2.61933 -0.50632 0);
    }

    bottom
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    frontAndBack
    {
        type            empty;
    }
}

fields
{
    U
    {
        type            fixedValue;
    }

    T
    {
        type            fixedValue;
    }

    p
    {
        type            fixedValue;
    }
}
```

This sets the initial velocity to the inlet value (2.9, 0, 0), temperature to 1.0 K, and pressure to 1.0 Pa everywhere, with the specified boundary conditions matching those in the `0/` files.

### Summary of Required Changes

1. **`0/T`**: Change `bottom` boundary condition from `zeroGradient` to `symmetryPlane`.
2. **`0/U`**: Change `bottom` boundary condition from `symmetryPlane` (already correct) — no change needed here.
3. **`0/p`**: Change `bottom` boundary condition from `extrapolatedCalculated` to `symmetryPlane`.
4. **Add `system/setFieldsDict`**: Create this file with initial and boundary conditions as shown above.

## Error Analysis and Resolution

### Error: `keyword regions is undefined in dictionary "system/setFieldsDict"`

**Error Message:**
```
keyword regions is undefined in dictionary "system/setFieldsDict"
```

**Root Cause:**
The `rhoCentralFoam` solver (OpenFOAM v10) expects a `regions` keyword in the `setFieldsDict` file to define the computational domain regions for field initialization. This is a newer version of OpenFOAM (v10) that uses a different format than older versions. The solver looks for a `regions` sub-dictionary that specifies which cell zones the initial and boundary conditions should be applied to.

**Solution:**
Add a `regions` sub-dictionary to the `system/setFieldsDict` file. The `regions` should contain the cell zone name (typically `internal` for the main domain) and reference the patches defined in the mesh. Here's what needs to be added:

In `system/setFieldsDict`, add the following `regions` sub-dictionary:

```
regions
{
    defaultPatch    patch;
    internal
    {
        type            cellZone;
        cells           ();
    }
}
```

The complete `setFieldsDict` should look like:

```
FoamFile
{
    version     2.0;
    format      ascii;
    class       dictionary;
    location    "system";
    object      setFieldsDict;
}

backgroundField   uniform (2.9 0 0);

patches
{
    inlet
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform (2.9 0 0);
    }

    outlet
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform (2.9 0 0);
    }

    top
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform (2.61933 -0.50632 0);
    }

    bottom
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    frontAndBack
    {
        type            empty;
    }
}

regions
{
    defaultPatch    patch;
    internal
    {
        type            cellZone;
        cells           ();
    }
}

fields
{
    U
    {
        type            fixedValue;
    }

    T
    {
        type            fixedValue;
    }

    p
    {
        type            fixedValue;
    }
}
```

**Additional Note:** The `bottom` boundary condition in `0/T` should remain `symmetryPlane` (as fixed in Attempt 1), and the `0/p` file should have `bottom` set to `symmetryPlane` instead of `extrapolatedCalculated` to match the mesh definition.

## Error Analysis and Resolution

### Error: Attempt to return dictionary entry as a primitive

**Error Message:**
```
Attempt to return dictionary entry as a primitive
```

**Root Cause:**
The error occurs in `setFieldsDict` at line 45-49, specifically in the `regions` sub-dictionary. In OpenFOAM v10, the `regions` dictionary format has changed. The `cells` keyword inside the `internal` cellZone sub-dictionary expects a **list of cell labels**, not an empty dictionary `()`. The empty dictionary `()` is being interpreted as a primitive value rather than a dictionary entry.

**Solution:**
In `system/setFieldsDict`, change the `cells` entry from `()` to an empty list `()`. The `cells` keyword should contain a list of vertex indices that define the cell zone. For an empty cell zone (which is valid for a mesh with no internal cells initially), use:

```
internal
{
    type            cellZone;
    cells           ();
}
```

However, the real issue is that the `cells` keyword expects a **list**, and `()` is being parsed as a primitive. The correct syntax is to use an empty list:

```
internal
{
    type            cellZone;
    cells           ();
}
```

But in OpenFOAM v10, the proper way is to use an empty list `()` which is actually a valid dictionary entry. The error suggests the parser is confused. The safest approach is to use the explicit empty list format:

```
internal
{
    type            cellZone;
    cells           ();
}
```
